*Purpose of our Community / Group*:-
How do we know islam is true? What Arguments have been Classically proposed for the truthfulness of Islam? Does Islam have any Rational Basis?Can Any Religion be proven or it required only faith? For Many Muslims we Automatically take the truthfulness of Islam Granted Many of us were born into Islam.We are told that God exists and that Allah (swt) send down Revelation in the form of books to Human being of a special status known as prophet. Naturally Some people's would Argue that if u weren't born a muslim and born into a Muslim family Would you have accepted islam would u have adopted whatever belief system your parents were upon?This is a good question and should make us all think To think about why we hold the beliefs that we hold Are there any good reasons to accept the belief we hold?

If so islam is true then what arguments are been proposed for the truthfulness of Islam And This is exactly the purpose of this group to articulate Reason and Arguments for fundamental beliefs of islam.
These Would be  the Main domains of Our Future Lecture Series and Books.
Way to beliefs

Epistemology 
Liberalism

Evidence for the Divine Origin of the Quran.
How to Give dawah to agnostics and Anti islamic People's And How to engage with them in Holistic way

11/5/23, 11:28â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: 1. i. With clear illustrations, give the definition of communication
ii. Explain five purposes of communication
iii. using a diagram ,explain the communication process
2. Explain five factors to consider when choosing a communication media
3. However careful one is when communicating, barriers will sometimes occur. Explain the
barriers to effective communication. 
4. Communication is a dynamic process of action and interaction towards a desired goal. 
Explain any four elements of communication process. 
5. Explain five principles of communication
6. There are different types of communication situations. In light of this sesntence, describe
upward, lateral, downward and grapevine communication. Give example in each
situation. 
7. Differentiate these two terms: interpersonal and intrapersonal communication.
11/5/23, 11:28â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: i. Communication is the process of sharing information, ideas, thoughts, or feelings between individuals or groups using verbal and non-verbal methods such as speaking, writing, gestures, or body language.

ii. Five purposes of communication include:

Informing: Sharing information, facts, or updates.
Persuading: Convincing or influencing others to adopt a certain point of view or take specific actions.
Expressing: Conveying emotions, thoughts, or feelings.
Instructing: Providing guidance or directions.
Building and Maintaining Relationships: Strengthening connections and bonds with others.
iii. Here's a simplified diagram of the communication process:
Sender -> Message -> Encoding -> Channel -> Decoding -> Receiver

Factors to consider when choosing a communication medium:

Purpose: Select a medium that aligns with your communication objectives.
Audience: Consider the preferences and accessibility of your target audience.
Urgency: Choose a medium that suits the time sensitivity of your message.
Complexity: Some messages may require richer media (e.g., face-to-face) for better understanding.
Cost and Resources: Evaluate the financial and logistical implications of the medium.
Barriers to effective communication can include:

Language barriers
Cultural differences
Noise and distractions
Emotional barriers (e.g., stress, bias)
Technical issues (e.g., poor reception or technology failures)
Four elements of the communication process:

Sender: The person initiating the message.
Message: The content being communicated.
Channel: The medium or method used to convey the message.
Receiver: The person who receives and interprets the message.
Principles of communication:

Clarity: Messages should be clear and easy to understand.
Listening: Effective communication involves active listening.
Feedback: Encouraging and receiving feedback enhances communication.
Non-Verbal Communication: Body language and tone convey additional meaning.
Context: Understanding the context of communication is crucial for accurate interpretation.
Types of communication situations include:

Upward Communication: Flow of information from subordinates to superiors, e.g., employee feedback to a manager.
Lateral Communication: Exchange of information between peers or colleagues, e.g., team members collaborating.
Downward Communication: Flow of information from superiors to subordinates, e.g., a manager providing instructions to employees.
Grapevine Communication: Informal, unofficial communication within an organization, often based on rumors or gossip.
Interpersonal communication refers to the exchange of information and emotions between two or more people. Intrapersonal communication is the process of self-communication, where an individual thinks, evaluates, and reflects on their thoughts and feelings within themselves.
11/5/23, 11:28â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: 1. Explain the features of quality listening
2. Differentiate between listening and hearing
3. Outline four qualities of a good listener
11/5/23, 11:29â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: Features of Quality Listening:

Active Engagement: Quality listening involves being fully present and engaged in the conversation, showing interest and attentiveness.
Empathy: Good listeners try to understand the speaker's perspective and emotions, showing empathy and support.
Avoiding Interruptions: They refrain from interrupting or interjecting while the speaker is talking, allowing them to express themselves fully.
Non-Verbal Cues: Quality listeners use non-verbal cues such as nodding, maintaining eye contact, and using appropriate body language to convey their attentiveness.
Asking Clarifying Questions: They ask relevant questions to gain a deeper understanding of the speaker's message.
Reflective Responses: Good listeners often provide thoughtful responses that reflect their understanding of what was said.
Difference between Listening and Hearing:

Listening is an active and intentional process that involves paying attention, processing, and interpreting the information received. It requires cognitive effort.
Hearing, on the other hand, is a passive and automatic process of perceiving sounds through the ears. It doesn't necessarily involve understanding or making sense of the sounds.
Qualities of a Good Listener:

Empathy: Good listeners are empathetic and strive to understand the speaker's emotions and perspective.
Patience: They are patient and give the speaker ample time to express themselves without rushing or interrupting.
Open-Mindedness: Good listeners maintain an open mind and are willing to consider different viewpoints without judgment.
Feedback: They provide constructive feedback and ask relevant questions to clarify or delve deeper into the conversation.
11/5/23, 11:30â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: 1. Describe two strategies you can use to improve each of the following:
a. Comprehension
b. Retention
2. Explain any three poor reading habits and provide a psychomotor reading strategy for
each. 
3. Mention any three discourse markers used in reading comprehensions and explain their
functions
4. Name any four types of paragraphs and give an example for each
5. Discuss how you would use the SQ3R reading formula to extract information from a book
6. Explain the following types of reading skills
a)scanning
b)skimming
c) critical reading
11/5/23, 11:30â€¯PM - Abdullah Tariq Cui: a. Strategies to Improve Comprehension:

Summarization: After reading a section, summarize what you've read in your own words. This helps reinforce understanding.
Active Questioning: While reading, ask yourself questions about the content. This encourages active engagement and comprehension.
b. Strategies to Improve Retention:

Note-Taking: Jot down key points, summaries, or important details as you read. This helps in retaining and recalling information.
Spaced Repetition: Review the material at intervals to reinforce memory. This technique can be helpful for long-term retention.
Three Poor Reading Habits and Psychomotor Reading Strategies:
a. Poor Habit: Subvocalization (silent reading while mouthing the words)
Psychomotor Strategy: Try to consciously reduce subvocalization by using a finger to guide your reading or by reading in short phrases.

b. Poor Habit: Regression (re-reading lines or sections)
Psychomotor Strategy: Place a card or paper under the line you're reading to block the previous lines, forcing you to move forward.

c. Poor Habit: Fixation (staring at one point for an extended time)
Psychomotor Strategy: Use your hand or a pointer to guide your eyes along the text, encouraging smoother eye movement.

Discourse Markers in Reading Comprehensions and Their Functions:

"Furthermore": This marker is used to add information or points to what was mentioned previously.
"However": It is used to introduce a contrast or a shift in the information.
"In conclusion": This marker signals the end of a section or the overall conclusion of the text.
Types of Paragraphs and Examples:

Expository Paragraph: Provides information or explanations. Example: A paragraph explaining the process of photosynthesis.
Narrative Paragraph: Tells a story or recounts events. Example: A paragraph describing a personal travel experience.
Descriptive Paragraph: Paints a vivid picture with details. Example: A paragraph describing a beautiful sunset.
Persuasive Paragraph: Conveys a viewpoint or argument. Example: A paragraph advocating for environmental conservation.
Using the SQ3R Reading Formula:

Survey: Quickly scan the material, read headings, subheadings, and summaries to get an overview.
Question: Formulate questions based on what you want to learn or understand.
Read: Actively read the material, looking for answers to your questions.
Recite: Summarize or verbally recall what you've learned.
Review: Go back to the material to reinforce your understanding and retention.
Types of Reading Skills:
a) Scanning: Rapidly looking for specific information or keywords in a text.
b) Skimming: Quickly glancing through a text to get an overall idea of its content.
c) Critical Reading: Analyzing and evaluating the text, considering the author's argument, evidence, and implications.

12/22/23, 10:21â€¯PM - +92 326 7780677: import java.io.File;
import java.io.FileNotFoundException;
import java.util.Scanner;

public class q3 {

    public static void main(String[] args) {

        Scanner input = new Scanner(System.in);

        System.out.print("Enter year: ");
        String year = input.next();

        System.out.print("Enter gender: ");
        String gender = input.next();

        System.out.print("Enter name: ");
        String name = input.next();
        input.close();

        File file = new File("babynamesranking" + year + ".txt");
        if (!file.exists()) {
            System.out.println("No record for " + year);
            System.exit(1);
        }

        int rank = 0;
        try {
            Scanner read = new Scanner(file);
            while (read.hasNext()) {

                String s = read.nextLine();
                String[] temp = s.split(" ");

                if (gender.equalsIgnoreCase("M") && temp[1].contains(name))
                    rank = new Integer(temp[0]);
                else if (temp[3].contains(name))
                    rank = new Integer(temp[0]);
            }
        } catch (FileNotFoundException e) {
            e.printStackTrace();
        }

        if (rank == 0) {
            System.out.println("The name "+name+" is not ranked in year " + year);
        } else {

            System.out.println(name+" is ranked #"+rank+" in year "+ year);
        }
    }
}

4/3/24, 8:47â€¯AM - alishakeel Cui: ### Calculation of Annual Loss Expectancy (ALE)

**Formula for ALE:**
\[ ALE = Annual Probability of Loss (APL) \times Single Loss Expectancy (SLE) \]

Given:
- APL (Annual Probability of Loss) = 10% = 0.1
- SLE (Single Loss Expectancy) without any mitigation = Rs150,000

\[ ALE = 0.1 \times Rs150,000 \]
\[ ALE = Rs15,000 \]

### Determining Risk Reduction Leverage for On-Site Security Guard

**Formula for Risk Reduction Leverage:**
\[ RRL = (Initial ALE - New ALE) / Initial ALE \]

Cost of On-Site Security Guard = Rs6,000 per month = Rs72,000 per year

**New ALE with Security Guard:**
\[ New ALE = APL \times (SLE - Cost of Security Guard) \]
\[ New ALE = 0.1 \times (Rs150,000 - Rs72,000) \]
\[ New ALE = 0.1 \times Rs78,000 \]
\[ New ALE = Rs7,800 \]

\[ RRL = (Rs15,000 - Rs7,800) / Rs15,000 \]
\[ RRL = 0.48 \] or \( 48\% \)

### Determining Risk Reduction Leverage for Surveillance System

Cost of Surveillance System = Rs3,000 per month = Rs36,000 per year

**New ALE with Surveillance System:**
\[ New ALE = APL \times (SLE \times 0.45) \] (55% reduction in loss)
\[ New ALE = 0.1 \times (Rs150,000 \times 0.45) \]
\[ New ALE = 0.1 \times Rs67,500 \]
\[ New ALE = Rs6,750 \]

\[ RRL = (Rs15,000 - Rs6,750) / Rs15,000 \]
\[ RRL = 0.55 \] or \( 55\% \)

### Comparison of Risk Reduction Leverages

| Measure                | Risk Reduction Leverage |
|------------------------|-------------------------|
| On-Site Security Guard | 48%                     |
| Surveillance System    | 55%                     |

### Conclusion

- If you choose the **On-Site Security Guard**, you can reduce the risk by **48%**.
- If you choose the **Surveillance System**, you can reduce the risk by **55%**.

**Based on the calculated risk reduction leverages, the Surveillance System seems to be a slightly better choice for risk reduction.**

1. Provide after-sales customer support

	â€¢	System Functionality: Payment processing system
	â€¢	Information Requirements: Customer payment information, security protocols for transactions, transaction history

Question 2: SWOT Analysis for an Online Bookstore

For a small online bookstore specializing in rare and collectible books:

Strengths (Internal)

	â€¢	Niche collection of rare books: Attracts specific segments of book collectors and enthusiasts, potentially enabling higher margins.

Weaknesses (Internal)

	â€¢	Limited technological resources: May struggle to compete with larger competitors on aspects like user experience, marketing reach, and advanced features like recommendation engines.

Opportunities (External)

	â€¢	Increase in e-book popularity: Can expand market reach and reduce costs associated with physical book storage and shipping. Offers potential for reaching a global audience.

4/17/25, 2:12â€¯PM - Uzair Ali Cui: Web Technologies Mid-Term Examination

Date: April 13, 2025

Course Learning Outcome (CLO): 2

Total Marks: 21 (Assumed based on Q1: 9, Q2: 9, Q3: 3)

Question 1 (9 Marks)
Theoretical Concepts in Web Technologies

a) Explain the benefits of using a layered architecture in web application development. Provide at least three advantages. (3 marks)

b) Define CSS combinators. List and briefly describe four types of combinators used in CSS. (3 marks)

c) What does it mean that "HTTP is a stateless protocol"? Illustrate with a practical example. (3 marks)

Question 2 (9 Marks)
Practical Application with HTML, CSS, and Bootstrap

a) Write HTML and CSS code to design a navigation bar with a background color, padding, and contrasting text color. Ensure the navigation links are horizontally aligned. (3 marks)

b) Create three buttons with different background colors (e.g., red, yellow, blue) using CSS. Apply padding, margin, and center-aligned text to each button. (3 marks)

c) Write a media query to transform a four-column layout into a single-column layout for screens smaller than 600px. Provide the necessary HTML and CSS for the columns. (3 marks)

Question 3 (3 Marks)
JavaScript Implementation with HTML5 (No CSS)

a) Write HTML5 and JavaScript code to automatically focus on the first input field of a form when the page loads. (1 mark)

b) Create a form with two fields (email and phone number). Use JavaScript to enable or disable the phone number field based on a checkbox selection. (1 mark)

c) Write JavaScript code to validate that an email input field contains a valid email format before form submission. Display an alert if the format is incorrect. (1 mark)
